# Reviewer template — per-experiment diff review (codex)

## Model + effort

`codex exec --model gpt-5.4 -c model_reasoning_effort=high`. Stdin
closed (`< /dev/null`) unless deliberately piping content.

Codex is **read-only** for reviewer use. It must not edit files.

## Log destination

`dev/plan/runs/<phase>-review-<utc-ts>.md`. The orchestrator commits
this file alongside the keep/revert decision so the audit trail
includes the review.

## Required reading + discipline (reviewer)

- **Read `AGENTS.md`** — canonical agent operating manual. Use it
  to judge whether the diff respects §1 invariants (TDD, ADRs,
  Public surface = contract, Stale > missing) and §5 test
  discipline. A diff that adds production code without a failing
  test first is a finding even if numbers look good.
- **Read `MEMORY.md`** and the `feedback_*.md` files; flag any
  diff that violates a rule encoded there.
- **Reviewer is read-only**. No file edits except the verdict file.
- **Do not run code**. Reviewer reads diffs and logs only.

## Context

- Plan: `dev/plan/0.6.0-Phase-9-Pack-5-performance-diagnostics.md` §0.1
  (reviewer mandate).
- Plan: §1 (acceptance for the packet).
- Per-phase prompt under `dev/plan/prompts/<phase>.md` —
  acceptance + decision rule live there.
- Implementer's run log:
  `dev/plan/runs/<phase>-<ts>.log`.
- Implementer's structured output:
  `dev/plan/runs/<phase>-output.json`.
- Diff under review: latest commit on the worktree branch
  `pack5-<phase>-<ts>`.

## Mandate

Read the diff and the implementer log. Issue a structured verdict.

### What to check

1. **Diff matches mandate**: every change traces to a mandate item in
   the per-phase prompt. Flag scope creep
   (extra files touched, refactors not requested, comments not
   asked for).
2. **Acceptance criteria from the per-phase prompt are met**: cite
   numbers from the implementer's output JSON. If the decision rule
   is numeric (e.g. concurrent ms drops by ≥ 30%), do the math
   yourself; do not trust the implementer's `decision_rule_met` flag
   without verification.
3. **AGENTS.md compliance**:
   - §1 invariants (TDD mandatory, ADRs authoritative, Public
     surface = contract).
   - §3 (was `agent-verify.sh` run? evidence in implementer log?).
   - §5 (failing test first; no test edits during fix-to-spec; no
     agent-generated oracles).
4. **TDD evidence**: a red-green-refactor cycle should be visible
   either in commit history or in the implementer log. Mechanical
   passes (pure rename, version bump) are exempt; behavior changes
   are not.
5. **`feedback_*` rules** (read MEMORY.md):
   - `feedback_cross_platform_rust.md` — c_char / c_int rule for any FFI.
   - `feedback_reliability_principles.md` — net-negative LoC bias.
   - `feedback_release_verification.md` — CI green is not done.
   - `feedback_tdd.md` — failing test first.
6. **Plan §5 cross-check**: no retry of any reverted experiment from
   `dev/notes/performance-whitepaper-notes.md` §5 without explicit
   override rationale in §12.

### Output shape (Markdown)

```markdown
# Review verdict — <phase> — <ts>

Verdict: PASS | CONCERN | BLOCK

## Summary
<2-4 sentence summary>

## Findings
1. <file:line> — <what> — <severity: nit | concern | block>
2. ...

## Acceptance criteria check
- <criterion 1>: PASS | FAIL — <evidence file:line or numbers>
- ...

## Decision-rule arithmetic
<show the math: numbers used, threshold, computed delta, met?>

## §5 retry cross-check
PASS | OVERRIDE-with-rationale: <text>

## Phase 7/8 invariants
PASS | CONCERN | BLOCK — <details>

## Recommended next step
<KEEP | REVERT | RUN_MORE_VERIFICATION | ESCALATE>
```

`PASS` = clean keep. `CONCERN` = orchestrator may keep but must
record the concern in §12. `BLOCK` = orchestrator must revert unless
they explicitly override with written rationale (per plan §0.1).

## Acceptance criteria (for the reviewer pass itself)

- Verdict is one of PASS / CONCERN / BLOCK; nothing else.
- Every finding cites `file:line`.
- Decision-rule arithmetic is shown.
- §5 retry cross-check is explicit.
- Phase 7/8 invariant cross-check (next file) is folded in OR
  delegated to a separate `review-phase78-robustness.md` invocation.

## Files allowed to touch

- `dev/plan/runs/<phase>-review-<utc-ts>.md` (the verdict file).

## Files NOT to touch

- Everything else. Reviewer is read-only.

## Verification commands

```bash
test -f dev/plan/runs/<phase>-review-<ts>.md
grep -E "^Verdict: (PASS|CONCERN|BLOCK)$" dev/plan/runs/<phase>-review-<ts>.md
```

## Required output to orchestrator

The Markdown file itself is the output. Orchestrator reads:

- `Verdict:` line.
- `Recommended next step:` line.
- `Findings` for any block-severity items.

## Required output to downstream agents

- None — reviewer feeds the orchestrator's keep/revert decision only.

## Update log

_(append the implementer's commit SHA, log path, and decision rule
before invoking codex)_
# Reviewer template — Phase 7/8 robustness check (codex)

## Model + effort

`codex exec --model gpt-5.4 -c model_reasoning_effort=high`. Stdin
closed (`< /dev/null`).

Read-only.

## Log destination

`dev/plan/runs/<phase>-review-phase78-<utc-ts>.md` (or appended to
the experiment review file from `review-experiment.md`).

## Required reading + discipline (reviewer)

- **Read `AGENTS.md`** — canonical agent operating manual. §1
  Public-surface-is-contract is the lens for this review: any
  weakening of a Phase 7/8 invariant is a contract regression.
- **Read `MEMORY.md` + `feedback_*.md`**.
- **Reviewer is read-only**. No file edits except the verdict file.

## Context

Phase 7 and Phase 8 of the 0.6.0 rewrite establish invariants that
later perf work must not weaken. This reviewer pass exists because
perf changes (especially FFI, mutex, and SQL refactors) are exactly
the kind of change that can silently break those invariants while
gates still go green on the perf side.

Plan §0.1 mandates this check for B.1 + D.1, optional but recommended
for B.2 / B.3 / C.1.

### Invariants to enforce

1. **Lifecycle event taxonomy** (REQ-006a / AC-005a / AC-007b):
   `Phase::Started`, `Finished`, `Failed`, with the correct
   `EventCategory` (Writer / Search / Admin / Error). The
   capture-ordinal-before-raise-ordinal contract for errors
   (AC-003d) — Failed/Error events fire **before** the
   `EngineError` returns to the caller.
   Code anchors:
   - `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs` write path:
     `write` at line 794, `write_inner` at line 831, error-emit
     ordering at line 818-826.
   - `Engine::search` at line 869, error-emit ordering at line
     880-895.
2. **Cursor-from-snapshot contract** (REQ-013 / AC-059b / REQ-055):
   `read_search_in_tx` derives `projection_cursor` from
   `load_projection_cursor` **inside** the `BEGIN DEFERRED` reader
   transaction (lib.rs:1283-1289). Result rows + cursor must be
   from the same snapshot.
3. **Profile-callback SAFETY** (commit `ba900a1`):
   - `ProfileContext` lives in `Box`es, not a `Vec<ProfileContext>`,
     because the FFI pointer must be stable
     (`Engine.profile_contexts: Mutex<Vec<Box<ProfileContext>>>` at
     lib.rs:77 — clippy-allowed `vec_box`).
   - `Box<ProfileContext>` outlives the connection that captured
     its pointer (drop order: connections drop first, then
     `profile_contexts`).
   - `install_profile_callback` (lib.rs:2401),
     `uninstall_profile_callback` (lib.rs:2436),
     `profile_callback_trampoline` (lib.rs:2457) — pointer
     lifetime invariants.
4. **Reader-pool ADR** (commits `09415b4`, `123a0d6`, `7852269`):
   - `READER_POOL_SIZE = 8` (lib.rs:48).
   - `ReaderPool` (lib.rs:158) must not serialize behind one mutex.
   - Each reader connection opens with `journal_mode=WAL` and
     `query_only=ON` (lib.rs:777-783).
5. **Database-lock-mechanism revision**:
   - Per-engine file lock (`Engine.lock: Mutex<Option<File>>`,
     lib.rs:54) — exclusive open contract preserved.
6. **Snapshot derivation in projection runtime**: the projection
   dispatcher / worker connections (`projection_dispatcher_loop` at
   lib.rs:1358, `projection_worker_loop` at lib.rs:1410) are
   long-lived and use `prepare_cached`; do not change their
   connection lifecycle without flagging.

# Review verdict — F.0 — 20260504T122055Z

Verdict: BLOCK

## Summary

F.0 matches the intended architectural intervention and it preserves the Phase 7/8 invariants I checked, but it does not meet the packet decision rule: `concurrent_median_ms=155` and `speedup=3.49x` both miss the KEEP thresholds and `155 > 100` hits the written REVERT rule. I also found two process violations and one contract violation: new always-`pub` test helpers expand the Rust surface without interface/ADR work, production edits landed before the first visible red test, and the implementer skipped `./scripts/agent-verify.sh` after checking the wrong path. `MEMORY.md` and local `feedback_*.md` files were not present in this worktree, so that part of the reviewer checklist could not be completed directly.

## Findings

1. `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:1175` — Adds new always-`pub` test helpers (`reader_worker_count_for_test`, `live_reader_worker_count_for_test`) without any companion interface-doc or ADR update, violating `AGENTS.md` public-surface rules and the F.0 prompt's "no public Rust API expansion" requirement — block
2. `/home/coreyt/projects/fathomdb/dev/plan/runs/F0-thread-affine-readers-20260504T115216Z.log:841` — Production edits to `src/lib.rs` are visible before the first creation of `tests/reader_pool.rs` at `...log:3515`, and the first visible red test failure is later at `...log:3624`; the branch therefore does not show failing-test-first TDD discipline — block

## Acceptance criteria check

- Authorized F.0 topology change: PASS — diff is limited to `src/lib.rs`, `tests/perf_gates.rs`, and `tests/reader_pool.rs`, and it introduces the private worker-pool/runtime types requested by the prompt (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:152`, `dev/plan/prompts/02-pack6-handoff-readerpool-refactor.md:85`)
- No hidden mutex on request dispatch hot path: PASS — dispatch is `AtomicUsize::fetch_add` plus per-worker `SyncSender::send`, with no global mutex on the request path (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:229`, `/home/coreyt/projects/fathomdb/dev/plan/runs/F0-thread-affine-readers-output.json:104`)
- Shutdown/integrity coverage landed: PASS — close/drop worker-exit tests are present and the structured output records them green (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/tests/reader_pool.rs:47`, `/home/coreyt/projects/fathomdb/dev/plan/runs/F0-thread-affine-readers-output.json:110`)

- Same-snapshot cursor contract preserved: PASS — `search_inner` still delegates to `read_search_in_tx`, and `read_search_in_tx` still loads `projection_cursor` inside the deferred read transaction (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:1059`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:1410`)

## Decision-rule arithmetic

KEEP requires `concurrent_median_ms <= 80` and `speedup >= 5.0x`; INCONCLUSIVE is only the `81..100 ms` band; REVERT triggers at `concurrent_median_ms > 100` (`dev/plan/prompts/02-pack6-handoff-readerpool-refactor.md:123`).

Observed medians from the structured output:

- `concurrent_median_ms = 155` (`/home/coreyt/projects/fathomdb/dev/plan/runs/F0-thread-affine-readers-output.json:91`)
- `speedup_median = 3.49x` (`/home/coreyt/projects/fathomdb/dev/plan/runs/F0-thread-affine-readers-output.json:97`)

Math:

- `155 - 100 = 55 ms` above the REVERT ceiling
- `155 - 80 = 75 ms` above the KEEP ceiling
- `5.0 - 3.49 = 1.51x` below the KEEP speedup floor

Result: decision rule not met for KEEP or INCONCLUSIVE; written REVERT rule is met.

PASS — this diff is the authorized F.0 thread-affine reader-worker intervention from the Pack 6 handoff, not a retry of reverted B.1 / C.1 / E.1 work (`dev/plan/prompts/02-pack6-handoff-readerpool-refactor.md:59`, `dev/notes/performance-whitepaper-notes.md:131`).

  2548	fn map_open_sqlite_error(err: rusqlite::Error, stage: OpenStage) -> EngineOpenError {
  2549	    let Some(sqlite_error) = err.sqlite_error() else {
  2550	        return EngineOpenError::Io { message: "could not open database".to_string() };
  2551	    };
  2552	    match sqlite_error.extended_code {
  2553	        rusqlite::ffi::SQLITE_CORRUPT | rusqlite::ffi::SQLITE_NOTADB => {
  2554	            EngineOpenError::Corruption(CorruptionDetail {
  2555	                kind: match stage {
  2556	                    OpenStage::WalReplay => CorruptionKind::WalReplayFailure,
  2557	                    OpenStage::HeaderProbe => CorruptionKind::HeaderMalformed,
  2558	                    OpenStage::SchemaProbe => CorruptionKind::SchemaInconsistent,
  2559	                    OpenStage::EmbedderIdentity => CorruptionKind::EmbedderIdentityDrift,
  2560	                },
  2561	                stage,
  2562	                locator: CorruptionLocator::OpaqueSqliteError {
  2563	                    sqlite_extended_code: sqlite_error.extended_code,
  2564	                },
  2565	                recovery_hint: RecoveryHint {
  2566	                    code: match stage {
  2567	                        OpenStage::WalReplay => "E_CORRUPT_WAL_REPLAY",
  2568	                        OpenStage::HeaderProbe => "E_CORRUPT_HEADER",
  2569	                        OpenStage::SchemaProbe => "E_CORRUPT_SCHEMA",
  2570	                        OpenStage::EmbedderIdentity => "E_CORRUPT_EMBEDDER_IDENTITY",
  2571	                    },
  2572	                    doc_anchor: match stage {
  2573	                        OpenStage::WalReplay => "design/recovery.md#wal-replay",
  2574	                        OpenStage::HeaderProbe => "design/recovery.md#header-format",
  2575	                        OpenStage::SchemaProbe => "design/recovery.md#schema-inconsistency",
  2576	                        OpenStage::EmbedderIdentity => "design/recovery.md#embedder-identity",
  2577	                    },
  2578	                },
  2579	            })
  2580	        }
  2581	        _ => EngineOpenError::Io { message: "could not open database".to_string() },
  2582	    }
  2583	}

  2585	fn emit_open_error_event(subscriber: &Arc<dyn lifecycle::Subscriber>, err: &EngineOpenError) {
  2586	    if let EngineOpenError::Corruption(detail) = err {
  2587	        let code = match detail.locator {
  2588	            CorruptionLocator::OpaqueSqliteError { sqlite_extended_code } => {
  2589	                Some(sqlite_extended_code_name_from_int(sqlite_extended_code))
  2590	            }
  2591	            _ => None,
  2592	        };
  2593	        let event = lifecycle::Event {
  2594	            phase: lifecycle::Phase::Failed,
  2595	            source: lifecycle::EventSource::SqliteInternal,
  2596	            category: lifecycle::EventCategory::Corruption,
  2597	            code,
  2598	        };
  2599	        subscriber.on_event(&event);
  2600	    }
  2601	}
  2602	
  2603	/// Install a `sqlite3_profile` callback on `connection` that dispatches
  2604	/// per-statement profile records and slow-statement signals to the
  2605	/// engine's subscriber registry.
  2606	///
  2607	/// Why FFI rather than `rusqlite::Connection::profile`: the safe API
  2608	/// (rusqlite 0.31) accepts only a `fn(&str, Duration)` with no
  2609	/// environment, so it cannot carry a per-engine subscriber-registry
  2610	/// pointer. We use `sqlite3_profile` directly with a leaked-into-`Box`
  2611	/// context whose pointer is tied to the engine's lifetime via
  2612	/// `Engine::profile_contexts`.
  2613	///
  2614	/// `sqlite3_profile` is documented as deprecated in favor of
  2615	/// `sqlite3_trace_v2`, but it remains supported and is sufficient for
  2616	/// the wall-clock + SQL-text payload required by AC-005a/b.
  2617	#[allow(clippy::vec_box)]
  2618	fn install_profile_callback(
  2619	    connection: &Connection,
  2620	    subscribers: &Arc<lifecycle::SubscriberRegistry>,
  2621	    profiling_enabled: &Arc<AtomicBool>,
  2622	    slow_threshold_ms: &Arc<AtomicU64>,
  2623	    contexts: &mut Vec<Box<ProfileContext>>,
  2624	) {
  2625	    let mut ctx = Box::new(ProfileContext {
  2626	        subscribers: Arc::clone(subscribers),
  2627	        profiling_enabled: Arc::clone(profiling_enabled),
  2628	        slow_threshold_ms: Arc::clone(slow_threshold_ms),
  2629	    });
  2630	    let ctx_ptr: *mut ProfileContext = &mut *ctx;
  2631	
  2632	    // SAFETY: the Box outlives the connection. Rust drops struct fields
  2633	    // in declaration order. `connection` and `reader_pool` are declared
  2634	    // before `profile_contexts`. `ReaderWorkerPool::Drop` joins every
  2635	    // reader worker, and each worker uninstalls and drops its owned
  2636	    // connection inside `reader_worker_loop` before the worker thread
  2637	    // returns. Therefore all connections — and SQLite's internal
  2638	    // profile-callback state with them — are torn down before the
  2639	    // `Box<ProfileContext>` allocations are freed. `Engine::close`
  2640	    // additionally clears the callback via
  2641	    // `sqlite3_profile(handle, None, NULL)` before connection close to
  2642	    // drain any in-flight callback dispatch.
  2643	    unsafe {
  2644	        rusqlite::ffi::sqlite3_profile(
  2645	            connection.handle(),
  2646	            Some(profile_callback_trampoline),
  2647	            ctx_ptr.cast::<std::ffi::c_void>(),
  2648	        );
  2649	    }
  2650	    contexts.push(ctx);
  2651	}
  2652	
  2653	/// Uninstall the profile callback so SQLite stops calling into our
  2654	/// freed `Box<ProfileContext>` pointer once a connection is being torn
  2655	/// down. Call before dropping `profile_contexts`.
  2656	fn uninstall_profile_callback(connection: &Connection) {
  2657	    // SAFETY: passing `None` as the callback unregisters the previous
  2658	    // callback; SQLite documents this as legal and idempotent.
  2659	    unsafe {
  2660	        rusqlite::ffi::sqlite3_profile(connection.handle(), None, std::ptr::null_mut());
  2661	    }
  2662	}
  2663

  2665	/// worker connection. Must be called BEFORE any statement is prepared

   930	        ensure_vector_partition(&connection, embedder_identity.dimension).map_err(|_| {

    24	5. SQLite reference: `https://www.sqlite.org/malloc.html` §3
    25	   "Lookaside Memory Allocator" — interface contract for
    26	   `sqlite3_db_config(SQLITE_DBCONFIG_LOOKASIDE, ...)`.
    27	6. Engine code:
    28	   - `crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs` — F.0 reader worker
    29	     `Connection::open` paths, profile-callback installation,
    30	     existing PRAGMAs applied per reader connection.
    31	   - `tests/perf_gates.rs`, `tests/reader_pool.rs`.
    32	
    33	## 2. Mandate (handoff §4 G.1 row)
    34	
    35	Configure SQLite per-connection lookaside on every F.0 reader
    36	worker connection, **immediately after open**, before any
    37	statement is prepared on that connection. Do **not** apply
    38	lookaside to the writer connection in this packet (writer is on
    39	the AC-018 / drain path, out of G.1 scope).
    40	
    41	Required call shape (per SQLite docs):
    42	
    43	```c
    44	sqlite3_db_config(db, SQLITE_DBCONFIG_LOOKASIDE, NULL, slot_size, slot_count);
    45	```
    46	
    47	Notes:
    48	
    49	- The middle pointer arg is a buffer the application supplies; pass
    50	  `NULL` to let SQLite allocate the lookaside backing memory itself.
    51	- Must be invoked before any other allocations on the connection,
    52	  per the SQLite docs. Place this call inside the worker's open
    53	  helper, ahead of the existing PRAGMAs that already run there.
    54	- `SQLITE_DBCONFIG_LOOKASIDE` is in `sqlite3.h` and exposed by
    55	  `libsqlite3-sys` via `ffi::SQLITE_DBCONFIG_LOOKASIDE` (or the
    56	  numeric value `1005` if the symbol is not surfaced — prefer the
    57	  named symbol when available).
    58	
    59	Use rusqlite's safe wrapper if it exists, else
    60	`unsafe { rusqlite::ffi::sqlite3_db_config(...) }` with the
    61	`Connection::handle()` raw pointer — rusqlite's `db_config`
    62	helper has historically been incomplete for the lookaside variant.
    63	Check rusqlite's API in this repo's `Cargo.lock` first; document
    64	which API path you used in the output JSON.
    65	
    66	Initial slot size / slot count: **1200 bytes × 500 slots** per
    67	worker (G.0 telemetry recommendation). If a quick sanity sweep is
    68	needed before committing, try the canonical grid below and pick
    69	the winner; do NOT bake the sweep into the production code path.
    70	
    71	| slot_size (bytes) | slot_count               |
    72	| ----------------- | ------------------------ |
    73	| 512               | 128 (default)            |
    74	| 512               | 500                      |
    75	| 1200              | 250                      |
    76	| 1200              | 500 (G.0 recommendation) |
    77	| 1200              | 1000                     |
    78	
    79	## 3. Required implementation shape
    80	
    81	1. Lookaside configuration is a private function on the reader
    82	   worker startup path. **No public Rust API expansion.** No new
    83	   `pub fn ..._for_test` accessors unless `#[cfg(debug_assertions)]`
    84	   gated and explicitly justified — F.0 reviewer block #1 standard.
    85	2. Preserve all current contracts: same-snapshot
    86	   `projection_cursor`, lifecycle / profiling / slow-signal
    87	   behavior, clean shutdown, AC-021 / AC-022, AC-018 drain.
    88	3. The lookaside call **must** complete before the worker installs
    89	   the profile callback or runs any PRAGMA. If the worker open
    90	   sequence is not ordered correctly, `SQLITE_DBCONFIG_LOOKASIDE`
    91	   will be silently ignored — capture the rc into a debug
    92	   assertion.
    93	4. FFI: `c_int` / `c_char` per memory `feedback_cross_platform_rust.md`.
    94	5. Use `./scripts/agent-verify.sh` (not `dev/agent-verify.sh`) per
    95	   F.0 reviewer block #3.
    96	
    97	## 4. Test discipline
    98	
    99	Red-green-refactor.
   100	
   101	Required new tests:
   102	
   103	1. Lookaside-applied test: an integration test that opens an
   104	   `Engine`, runs a small read, and asserts (via
   105	   `sqlite3_db_status(... SQLITE_DBSTATUS_LOOKASIDE_USED, ...)` per
   106	   `https://www.sqlite.org/c3ref/c_dbstatus_options.html`) that at
   107	   least one lookaside slot was consumed on each reader worker
   108	   connection. Use a `#[cfg(debug_assertions)]`-gated test helper
   109	   if needed; do not expand the public surface.
   110	2. Lookaside-ordering test: assert that
   111	   `sqlite3_db_config(LOOKASIDE)` was called before any
   112	   `prepare_*` / `execute_*` on the worker connection (otherwise
   113	   the configuration is silently ignored). The cleanest form is a
   114	   counter assertion: at the moment lookaside is configured,
   115	   `SQLITE_DBSTATUS_LOOKASIDE_USED` is 0; after the first read it
   116	   is > 0; after the test the rc of the original config call was
   117	   `SQLITE_OK`.
   118	3. AC-017 / AC-018 / AC-021 / AC-022 / AC-059b cursor / read-
   119	   snapshot coverage stays green unchanged.
   120

   125	   JSON.

   129	6. `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt
   130	--check`.

   117	    "lever": "G.1",
   118	    "rationale": "allocator_lookaside is 26.67% of conc cycles with ratio 3.89 vs sequential and a +145.7M-cycle delta (the largest absolute contention delta in the profile). The hot stacks are sqlite3DbMallocRaw / sqlite3Malloc.part.0 -> __GI___libc_malloc / __libc_free, with pthread_mutex contention on the glibc malloc arena. This is exactly the documented happy-path for SQLite's per-connection lookaside (https://www.sqlite.org/malloc.html §3): a sticky long-lived reader connection is the right amortization shape, and F.0 just made every reader connection sticky for life. Lookaside satisfies most small allocations from a per-connection arena, drops the rate of __libc_malloc calls, and removes the glibc arena mutex from the hot path.  succeeded in 0ms:
  2660	        rusqlite::ffi::sqlite3_profile(connection.handle(), None, std::ptr::null_mut());
  2661	    }

  2663	
  2664	/// Pack 6.G G.1 — configure SQLite per-connection lookaside on a reader
  2665	/// worker connection. Must be called BEFORE any statement is prepared
  2666	/// or any PRAGMA is run on `connection`; per the SQLite docs
  2667	/// (https://www.sqlite.org/malloc.html §3) lookaside is silently
  2668	/// ignored if reconfigured after the first allocation on the
  2669	/// connection. Passing `NULL` for the buffer pointer lets SQLite
  2670	/// allocate the lookaside backing memory itself.
  2671	///
  2672	/// rusqlite 0.31's `set_db_config` only handles the boolean
  2673	/// `DbConfig::*` variants; `SQLITE_DBCONFIG_LOOKASIDE` is not surfaced
  2674	/// (it is commented out in `rusqlite/src/config.rs`), so we call the
  2675	/// raw FFI directly.
  2676	///
  2677	/// Returns the rc of `sqlite3_db_config` so callers can debug-assert
  2678	/// `SQLITE_OK` and surface configuration failure under
  2679	/// `debug_assertions` test builds without expanding the public surface.
  2680	fn configure_reader_lookaside(connection: &Connection) -> std::os::raw::c_int {
  2681	    // SAFETY: `connection.handle()` returns a valid `*mut sqlite3` for
  2682	    // the lifetime of `connection`. The variadic
  2683	    // `sqlite3_db_config(LOOKASIDE)` call expects three trailing
  2684	    // arguments of types `void*`, `int`, `int` — the prototype shape
  2685	    // documented in `sqlite3.h`. We pass a null buffer so SQLite owns
  2686	    // the lookaside backing allocation, and the slot size / count from
  2687	    // the G.1 constants. No allocations happen on the connection
  2688	    // before this call (reader open path is `Connection::open` ->
  2689	    // `configure_reader_lookaside` -> first PRAGMA).
  2690	    unsafe {
  2691	        rusqlite::ffi::sqlite3_db_config(
  2692	            connection.handle(),
  2693	            rusqlite::ffi::SQLITE_DBCONFIG_LOOKASIDE,
  2694	            std::ptr::null_mut::<std::ffi::c_void>(),
  2695	            READER_LOOKASIDE_SLOT_SIZE,
  2696	            READER_LOOKASIDE_SLOT_COUNT,
  2697	        )
  2698	    }
  2699	}
  2700	
  2701	/// Read the high-water-mark for `SQLITE_DBSTATUS_LOOKASIDE_USED` on
  2702	/// `connection`. The `current` out-param is the live checked-out slot
  2703	/// count and decays as transactions finalize, so it is unreliable as
  2704	/// post-warmup evidence. The `hiwtr` out-param latches the largest
  2705	/// observed `current` value since the last reset and is the right
  2706	/// signal that lookaside was honored at any point on this connection.
  2707	/// Reset flag is `0` so reading does not clear the high-water mark.
  2708	#[cfg(debug_assertions)]
  2709	fn read_lookaside_used_hiwtr(connection: &Connection) -> std::os::raw::c_int {
  2710	    let mut current: std::os::raw::c_int = 0;
  2711	    let mut hiwtr: std::os::raw::c_int = 0;
  2712	    // SAFETY: handle is valid; both out pointers are to local stack
  2713	    // ints; reset flag 0 is documented as legal.
  2714	    unsafe {
  2715	        rusqlite::ffi::sqlite3_db_status(

+# Review verdict — G.1 — 20260504T141437Z
+
+Verdict: CONCERN
+
+## Summary
+
+G.1 matches the intended lookaside-tuning mandate, keeps the change set narrow, and preserves the Phase 7/8 invariants I checked. The numeric rule supports the implementer's `INCONCLUSIVE` self-decision: `concurrent_median_ms` improved from `168` to `161`, but the KEEP threshold was `156.11`, so the measured gain stays inside the G.0 noise band while `speedup_median` improves from `3.339x` to `3.530x`. `MEMORY.md` and local `feedback_*.md` files were not present in this worktree, so that part of the reviewer checklist could not be completed directly.
+
+## Findings
+
+1. `dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:8` — The red phase is only self-reported in the output JSON; the branch history shows a single green code commit and there is no committed `dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-20260504T135138Z.log`, so failing-test-first TDD is not independently auditable from the artifacts required by the reviewer template and `AGENTS.md` §1/§5 — concern
+2. `dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:111` — The claimed `./scripts/agent-verify.sh` pass is likewise only self-reported because the expected per-phase implementer log is absent, which weakens the audit trail for `AGENTS.md` §3 compliance even though the structured output says verify passed — concern
+3. `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:211` — The new `ReaderRequest::LookasideStatus` comment says the request returns the lookaside “current value,” but the implementation intentionally returns the high-water mark via `read_lookaside_used_hiwtr` (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:2701`); under `AGENTS.md` “stale > missing,” this comment is misleading — nit
+
+## Acceptance criteria check
+
+- Diff matches G.1 mandate: PASS — the code change is limited to reader-worker lookaside wiring plus the two requested integration tests (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:947`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/tests/reader_pool.rs:147`).
+- Lookaside is configured immediately after reader `Connection::open` and before any reader PRAGMA or profile-callback installation: PASS — `configure_reader_lookaside` runs at open time before `journal_mode=WAL` / `query_only=ON`, and reader profile callbacks are installed only after `open_locked` returns (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:947`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:861`).
+- No writer-side lookaside change: PASS — the writer open path remains unchanged and the new call is only in the reader loop inside `open_locked` (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:917`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:947`).
+- No public Rust API expansion beyond the accepted debug-only convention: PASS — the new helpers are `#[cfg(debug_assertions)]` and `#[doc(hidden)]`, matching the F.0 reviewer convention (`dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:81`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:1257`).
+- Required G.1 test coverage landed: PASS — one test asserts `SQLITE_OK` rc per worker and one asserts post-warmup lookaside use per worker (`dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:103`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/tests/reader_pool.rs:147`).
+- AC-017 and AC-018 stay green: PASS — the output JSON records AC-017 passed and AC-018 drain `95 ms` (`dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:32`, `dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:39`).
+- Decision rule for KEEP: FAIL — `161 ms` does not beat the `156.11 ms` threshold, although the ratio floor passes (`dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:195`, `dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:79`).
+- Decision rule for INCONCLUSIVE: PASS — the measured improvement is within one G.0 standard deviation while `speedup_median` stays above baseline, matching the written `INCONCLUSIVE` lane (`dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:199`, `dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:73`).
+
+## Decision-rule arithmetic
+
+G.1 imports the G.0 baseline-of-record `concurrent_median_ms = 168`, `concurrent_stddev = 11.89`, `speedup_median = 3.339x` (`dev/plan/runs/G0-wal-checkpoint-telemetry-output.json:40`, `dev/plan/runs/G0-wal-checkpoint-telemetry-output.json:42`, `dev/plan/runs/G0-wal-checkpoint-telemetry-output.json:35`). The G.1 prompt says KEEP requires `concurrent_median_ms < baseline - 1×stddev` and `speedup_median >= baseline` (`dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:195`).
+
+Math:
+
+- KEEP latency threshold = `168 - 11.89 = 156.11 ms`
+- Observed G.1 `concurrent_median_ms = 161 ms` (`dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:68`)
+- Margin vs KEEP threshold = `161 - 156.11 = 4.89 ms` missed
+- Observed G.1 `speedup_median = 3.530x` (`dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:69`)
+- Ratio delta vs baseline = `3.530 - 3.339 = +0.191x`
+
+Result: KEEP is not met, REVERT is not triggered by the written numeric rule, and the artifacts support `INCONCLUSIVE`.
+
+## §5 retry cross-check
+
+PASS — lookaside is explicitly authorized for G.1 and is not one of the whitepaper §5 do-not-retry experiments; the output JSON also records no re-run of B.1 / C.1 / E.1 / cache-size / `NO_MUTEX` work (`dev/notes/performance-whitepaper-notes.md:170`, `dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:137`, `dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:113`).
+
+## Phase 7/8 invariants
+
+PASS — lifecycle event taxonomy is untouched because `write` / `search` paths were not modified by this diff; the cursor-from-snapshot contract still loads `projection_cursor` inside the deferred reader transaction (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:1500`); profile-callback SAFETY still relies on `Mutex<Vec<Box<ProfileContext>>>` and unchanged install/uninstall ordering (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:93`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:2618`); the reader-pool ADR still holds with `READER_POOL_SIZE = 8` and reader `WAL`/`query_only` PRAGMAs intact (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:49`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:962`); the per-engine file lock is unchanged (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:70`); and the projection-runtime connection lifecycle is unchanged because none of the dispatcher/worker connection code moved in this patch.
+
+## Recommended next step
+
+RUN_MORE_VERIFICATION

+## Acceptance criteria check
+
+- Diff matches G.1 mandate: PASS — the code change is limited to reader-worker lookaside wiring plus the two requested integration tests (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:947`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/tests/reader_pool.rs:147`).
+- Lookaside is configured immediately after reader `Connection::open` and before any reader PRAGMA or profile-callback installation: PASS — `configure_reader_lookaside` runs at open time before `journal_mode=WAL` / `query_only=ON`, and reader profile callbacks are installed only after `open_locked` returns (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:947`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:861`).
+- No writer-side lookaside change: PASS — the writer open path remains unchanged and the new call is only in the reader loop inside `open_locked` (`src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:917`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:947`).
+- No public Rust API expansion beyond the accepted debug-only convention: PASS — the new helpers are `#[cfg(debug_assertions)]` and `#[doc(hidden)]`, matching the F.0 reviewer convention (`dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:81`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/src/lib.rs:1257`).
+- Required G.1 test coverage landed: PASS — one test asserts `SQLITE_OK` rc per worker and one asserts post-warmup lookaside use per worker (`dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:103`, `src/rust/crates/fathomdb-engine/tests/reader_pool.rs:147`).
+- AC-017 and AC-018 stay green: PASS — the output JSON records AC-017 passed and AC-018 drain `95 ms` (`dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:32`, `dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:39`).
+- Decision rule for KEEP: FAIL — `161 ms` does not beat the `156.11 ms` threshold, although the ratio floor passes (`dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:195`, `dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:79`).
+- Decision rule for INCONCLUSIVE: PASS — the measured improvement is within one G.0 standard deviation while `speedup_median` stays above baseline, matching the written `INCONCLUSIVE` lane (`dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:199`, `dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:73`).

+## Decision-rule arithmetic
+
+G.1 imports the G.0 baseline-of-record `concurrent_median_ms = 168`, `concurrent_stddev = 11.89`, `speedup_median = 3.339x` (`dev/plan/runs/G0-wal-checkpoint-telemetry-output.json:40`, `dev/plan/runs/G0-wal-checkpoint-telemetry-output.json:42`, `dev/plan/runs/G0-wal-checkpoint-telemetry-output.json:35`). The G.1 prompt says KEEP requires `concurrent_median_ms < baseline - 1×stddev` and `speedup_median >= baseline` (`dev/plan/prompts/G1-reader-lookaside.md:195`).
+
+Math:
+
+- KEEP latency threshold = `168 - 11.89 = 156.11 ms`
+- Observed G.1 `concurrent_median_ms = 161 ms` (`dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:68`)

+- Observed G.1 `speedup_median = 3.530x` (`dev/plan/runs/G1-reader-lookaside-output.json:69`)
+- Ratio delta vs baseline = `3.530 - 3.339 = +0.191x`
+

+

+
